тАШ рдХрд╛ рд╕реБрд╖реНрдЯреБрддрд┐рдГ’ рдЗрддреНрдпреЗрдХрд╛рджрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдВ рддреГрддреАрдпрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╡рд╛рдорджреЗрд╡рд╕реНрдпрд╛рд░реНрд╖рдореИрдиреНрджреНрд░рдореН ред рджрд╢рдореНрдпрдиреБрд╖реНрдЯреБрдкреН рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдГред рддрдерд╛ рдЪрд╛рдиреБрдХреНрд░рдордгрд┐рдХрд╛- рдХрд╛ рд╕реБрд╖реНрдЯреБрддрд┐рд░реБрдкрд╛рдиреНрддреНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╖реНрдЯреБрдкреН ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧреЛ рд▓реИрдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдХрдГ рее

Jamison Brereton

24 (320)
Indra
V─Бmadeva Gautama
11 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except anuс╣гс╣нubh 10
For most of its length (vss. 1тАУ7), this hymn expresses in vivid language the familiar notion of competing parties invoking Indra for help and offering him sacrificial oblations and praise in return. Verses 3тАУ5 are especially focused on the desperate efforts of the human antagonists to enlist IndraтАЩs might on their own side. It is also clear that the offerings made by the successful supplicants must be made just so: in addition to soma, a whole sacrificial menu is specified, with a special emphasis on cooked foods (see esp. vss. 5, 7).
The last three verses (8тАУ10, before the V─Бmadeva refrain in 11) lay bare the mecha nism of the divineтАУhuman bargain that lies behind the first part of the hymn, and indeed behind the whole R╠еgvedic enterprise more generally. Rather than casting the exchange relations between men and gods in the rosy light of mutual benefit and voluntary cooperation, the verses present the acquisition of IndraтАЩs aid by mortals as a matter of cold-blooded haggling and crass calculations of price versus value received. In our interpretation, Indra even has an agent, in the person of his own wife. These verses are difficult, enigmatic, and apparently use the lexicon and phraseology of commercial transactions, a linguistic level barely attested elsewhere in Vedic. Consequently the meaning of the verses is much disputed, and we will provide here only our own interpretation (which follows GeldnerтАЩs in many, but not all, ways).
In verse 8 Indra (or perhaps his wife, a possibility raised by Oldenberg and Geldner) takes a long hard look at the hostilities heтАЩs being asked to participate in, and his wife calls him back home, presumably to sit out the conflict or at least to hold out for a better offer. In fact, in verse 9 Indra reports on a failed bit of hag
gling. An unidentified party seems to have made a bad deal, offering a higher price for an inferior product, in this case probably the help of a god less powerful than Indra (9a). With IndraтАЩs own offer not accepted, he goes happily home тАЬunsoldтАЭ (9b), remarking that the other party did not seize his chance to replace the inferior product with a greater one, namely Indra himself (9c). He ends with what appears to be a maxim, mocking the negotiation prowess of the other party (9d). Verse 10, in our view (and ours alone?), is spoken by IndraтАЩs wife, hawking her husband and his obstacle-smashing talent and naming her price for his sale. The price, ten cows, seems very low for such a god (especially considering how many hundreds of cows are elsewhere given to mortal poets and priests, at least according to d─Бnastutis), and so it is possible or even likely that this is a bitter and rhetorical question, com plaining about the stinginess of mortal purchasers. In any case, itтАЩs a limited-term offer, as she expects Indra to be returned at the end of his mercenary service.
The allusion to d─Бnastutis above was purposeful, for this little set of verses not only occupies the position of a d─Бnastuti in this hymn, but also has the slangy and derisory tone of many d─Бnastutis and the same recognition of the commer cial underpinnings of the relationship between patron and client. It may even be that, using IndraтАЩs withdrawal as model, the poet is indirectly complaining about an ungenerous patron and threatening to withhold his poetic production unless he receives a better deal.

Jamison Brereton Notes

рдХрд╛ рдХреАрджреГрд╢реА рд╕реБрд╖реНрдЯреБрддрд┐рдГ рд╢рд╡рд╕рдГ рд╕реВрдиреБрдВ рдмрд▓рд╕реНрдп рдкреБрддреНрд░рдореН ред рдЕрддрд┐рдмрд▓рд┐рдирдорд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдЕрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдЪреАрдирдореН рдЕрд╕реНрдорджрднрд┐рдореБрдЦрдореН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдВ рдкрд░рдореИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдпреБрдХреНрддрдВ рд░рд╛рдзрд╕реЗ рдзрдирд╛рдп рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдВ рдзрдирдВ рджрд╛рддреБрдореН рдЖ рд╡рд╡рд░реНрддрддреН рдЖрд╡рд░реНрддрдпреЗрддреН ред рд╣реЗ рдЬрдирд╛рд╕рдГ рдЬрдирд╛ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рд╡реАрд░рдГ рд╡рд┐рдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдГ рдЧреЛрдкрддрд┐рдГ рдкрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рдзрдирд╕реНрдп рдкрд╛рд▓рдХрдГ рд╕рдГ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдирд┐рд╖реНрд╖рд┐рдзрд╛рдВ рдирд┐рд╖реНрд╖реЗрджреНрдзреДрдгрд╛рдВ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдгрд╛рдВ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзреАрдирд┐ рд╡рд╕реВрдирд┐ рдзрдирд╛рдирд┐ рдЧреГрдгрддреЗ рдЧреГрдгрджреНрднреНрдпрдГ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреГрднреНрдпрдГ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдВ рджрджрд┐рд░реНрд╣рд┐ рджрд╛рддрд╛ рдЦрд▓реБ рднрд╡рддрд┐ ред

English translation:

тАЬWhat suitable praise may bring the son of strength, Indra, before us, to give us wealth; the hero, the lord of cattle, is the donor, oс╕е man, of the wealth of his adversaries to him who glorifies him.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

What good praise will turn Indra hereтАФthe son of strength, facing our wayтАФfor our benefit?
For the hero is the giver of good things to the singer, and he is the
herdsman of our tribute, o peoples.

Griffith

WHAT worthy praise will bring before us Indra, the Son of Strength, that he may grant us riches;
For he the Hero, gives the singer treasures: he is the Lord who sends us gifts, ye people.

Geldner

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe, Indra, is to be invoked for the destruction of Vс╣Ыtra; he, the deservedly praised, is to be worshipped; the real donor of wealth, he, Maghavan, gives wealth, (acquired) in battle, to the mortal offers him prayer and libations.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He is to be summoned at the smashing of obstacles, he is to be invoked, and he is well praisedтАФIndra, whose benefit is real.
Here on his journey the bounteous one establishes wide space for the mortal soma-presser devoted to the sacred formulation.

Griffith

To be invoked and hymned in fight with Vrtra, that well-praised Indra gives us real bounties.
That Maghavan brings comfort in the foray to the religious man who pours libations.

Geldner

Er ist in der Schlacht anzurufen, er aufzubieten. Indra ist der Sch├╢ngepriesene, dessen Gaben echt sind. Der Freigebige soll auf seiner Fahrt dem segensprechenden, somapressenden Sterblichen einen Ausweg aus der Not schaffen.

Grassmann

Er ist zu rufen, anzuflehn im Kampfe, der hochgelobte, wahrhaft reiche Indra; Er schenke Fortgang auf der Fahrt dem Menschen, der m├дchtige dem frommen Somapresser.

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

рдирд░рдГ рдиреЗрддрд╛рд░реЛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдГ рд╕рдореАрдХреЗ рдпреБрджреНрдзреЗ рддрдорд┐рддреН рддрдореЗрд╡реЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдВ рд╡рд┐ рд╣реНрд╡рдпрдиреНрддреЗ рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдзрдорд╛рд╣реНрд╡рд╛рдирдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рддреЗ ред рддрдиреНрд╡рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рдХреАрдпрд╛рдирд┐ рд╢рд░реАрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рд░рд┐рд░рд┐рдХреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕рдГ рддрдкрд╕рд╛ рд░реЗрдЪрдпрдиреНрддреЛ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡реЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдВ рддреНрд░рд╛рдВ рддреНрд░рд╛рддрд╛рд░рдВ рдХреГрдгреНрд╡рдд рдХреГрдгреНрд╡рддреЗ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рддреЗ ред рдпрддреН рдпрджрд╛ рдорд┐рдердГ рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рдВ рд╕рдВрдЧрддрд╛рдГ рдЙрднрдпрд╛рд╕рдГ рдЙрднрдпреЗ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рд╕реНрддреЛрддрд╛рд░рд╢реНрдЪ рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧрдВ рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧрдХрд░реНрддрд╛рд░рдВ рджрд╛рддрд╛рд░рдорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдореН рдЕрдЧреНрдордиреН рдЙрдкрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ рддрджрд╛ рдирд░рдГ рдЙрднрдпрд╡рд┐рдзрд╛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдГ рддреЛрдХрд╕реНрдп рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рддрдирдпрд╕реНрдп рдкреМрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рдЪ рд╕рд╛рддреМ рд▓рд╛рднреЗ рдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддрднреВрддреЗ рд╕рддрд┐ рддрдореЗрд╡реЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдВ рддреНрд░рд╛рддрд╛рд░рдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддреАрддрд┐ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMen verily call upon him in battle; the (devout) inflicters of austerity upon their person ns constitute him their preserver; when both (the worshipper and the priest) approach together the bountiful Indra, men (succeed) in (obtaining) the gift of sons and grandsons.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Inflicters of austerity: ririkv─Бс╣Гsas tanaс╕е = svak─лy─Бni ┼Ыar─лr─Бс╣Зi tapas─Б recayanto yajam─Бn─Бс╕е, worshippers emaciating their own bodies by penance

Jamison Brereton

Just to him do men separately call at the encounter. Having given up their bodies, they make him their preserver,
when the men of both camps, on opposite sides, have come to abandon (their bodies) in the winning of offspring and descendants.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Most depictions of battle in the RV do not frame the risks of entering into battle quite so starkly. Here both ririkv─Б╠Бс╣Гsas tanv├ас╕е тАЬhaving given up their bodiesтАЭ in b and ty─Бg├бm тАж ├бgman тАЬhave come to the abandonment (of their bodies, presumably)тАЭ in c seem to refer to a sort of resignation in the face of death and a loss of the sense of self. (Note that this is the only occurrence of ty─Б╠Бga- in the RV.) It is esp. telling that they give up their own bodies to gain offspring and a long line of descendants. For the similarity between this passage and the T─Бn┼лnaptra ritual, see Proferes (58).

Griffith

Him, verily, the men invoke in combat; risking their lives they make him their protector,
When heroes, foe to foe, give up their bodies, fighting, each side, for children and their offspring.

Geldner

Nur ihn rufen die M├дnner in der Schlacht von beiden Seiten; ihre Leiber hingebend machen sie ihn zu ihrem Hort, wenn die beiderseitigen M├дnner sich gegenseitig aufopfern, um leiblichen Samen zu gewinnen.

Grassmann

Ihn rufen an die M├дnner in dem Kampfe; sie machten Leben wagend ihn zum Sch├╝tzer, Als Freund und Feind zum Todeskampfe eilten, die M├дnner, zu besch├╝tzen Kind und Enkel.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPowerful Indra, men variously dispersed, come mutually together to celebrate sacred rites for the sake of obtaining rain; when men who are combatants assemble in battle, there are some of them who rely upon Indra.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The settled peoples show their resolve at the hitching up (for battle), o powerful one, while they are gasping on opposite sides in the winning of the flood.

When the battling clans have rolled together, just then do those on the one side seek Indra at the moment of confrontation.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The тАШwinning of the floodтАЩ (├бrс╣Зas─Бtau) presumably refers, as Geldner, etc., point out, to the battle to control water resources, esp. dwelling places near water.

Most tr. give a more neutral rendering of ├бvavс╣Ыtranta, but my тАЬhave rolled togetherтАЭ is meant to convey the deeply entwined, rough-and-tumble quality of pitched battle (and, perhaps, the actual rolling of chariots onto the battlefield).

Jamison Brereton Notes

The pile-up of p─Бda-initial ─Б╠Бd ├нd тАШjust then, just after thatтАЩ, beginning with 4d and marking every p─Бda in 5, conveys the quick succession of events, but switches abruptly from battlefield to sacrifice. The n├йme constructions of 4d and 5a make it clear, however, that despite the change in venue the same antagonists are in play.

Note also the similarity of the predicates of the two n├йme constructions: indrayante тАж indriy├бс╣Г yajante. This is the only occurrence of the denom. indraya- in the RV and it may have been created to serve as a foil for the second VP.

Griffith

Strong God! the folk at need put forth their vigour, striving together in the whirl of battle.
When warrior bands encounter one another some in the grapple quit themselves like Indra.

Geldner

Die V├╢lker sinnen auf Kriegsfahrt, du Gewaltiger, gegenseitig sich aneifernd zum Kampf um Wasserpl├дtze. Wenn die streitbaren St├дmme aneinandergeraten sind, dann verlangen die einen im entscheidenden Augenblick nach Indra.

Grassmann

Die V├╢lker m├╝hn sich bei dem Werk, o Starker, im Kampfgew├╝hle aufeinander schnaubend; Wenn handgemein der Streiter Scharen wurden, dann wirken diese Indra-gleich im Treffen.

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

рдЖрджрд┐рддреН рддрджрд╛рдиреАрдореЗрд╡ рдпреБрджреНрдзрдХрд╛рд▓реЗ рдиреЗрдореЗ рдЕрдиреНрдпреЗ рдпреЛрдзрд╛рдГ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдпрдВ рдмрд▓рд╡рдиреНрддрдорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдВ рдпрдЬрдиреНрддреЗ рд╣ рдкреВрдЬрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рдЦрд▓реБ ред рдХрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рддреН рдЖрджрд┐рддреН рдЕрдирдиреНрддрд░рдореЗрд╡ рдкреБрд░реЛрд│рд╛рд╢рдВ рдкрд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд░реВрдкрдВ рд╣рд╡рд┐рдГ рдкрдХреНрддрд┐рдГ рдкрдЪрдиреН рд░рд┐рд░рд┐рдЪреНрдпрд╛рддреН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдп рджрджреНрдпрд╛рддреН ред рдЖрджрд┐рддреН рдЕрдирдиреНрддрд░рдореЗрд╡ рд╕реЛрдордГ рдЕрднрд┐рд╖реБрддрд╕реЛрдореЛ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реБрд╖реНрд╡реАрдиреН рдЕрдирднрд┐рд╖реБрддрд╕реЛрдорд╛рдиреН рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдиреН рд╡рд┐ рдкрдкреГрдЪреНрдпрд╛рддреН рдзрдиреИрдГ рдкреГрдердХреНрдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рддреН ред рдЖрджрд┐рддреН рдЕрдирдиреНрддрд░рдореЗрд╡ рдХрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рддреН рд╡реГрд╖рднрдВ рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рд┐рддрд╛рд░рдорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдВ рдпрдЬрдзреНрдпреИ рдпрд╖реНрдЯреБрдВ рдЬреБрдЬреЛрд╖ рд╕реЗрд╡рддреЗ рее рее резрез рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThereupon some verily worship the powerful (Indra); thereupon one man prepares the buttered cake that he may offer it to (Indra); thereupon the offerer of the Soma he distinguishes from him who presents no libation; thereupon some one rejoices to worship the showerer (of benefits).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Just then do those on the other side perform sacrifice to his Indrian strength; just then would the cooked food succeed the offering cake;
just then would soma exclude the non-pressers; and just then does he [=Indra] find pleasure in the bull [=soma] for the sacrifice to proceed.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The bridge between 4d and 5a has already been noted, as well as the change of scene. However, I think the competition visible in vss. 3-4, as well as in vss. 6-7, continues here by other, sacrificial, means. To get Indra on their side in battle, the men must perform not only a correct sacrifice, but a better sacrifice. One puzzling feature of this vs. is the presence of pf. optatives in p─Бdas b and c. As I have discussed elsewhere (2008 тАЬWomenтАЩs Language in the RVтАЭ [Ged. Elizarenkova], 2009 тАЬWhere Are All the OptativesтАЭ [East and West]), the pf. opt. has a curious distribution and, to some extent, a particular sociolinguistic profile, and it is not clear what riricy─Бt (b) and v├н papс╣Ыcy─Бt (c) are doing sandwiched between a pres. (yajante, a) and a presential perfect (jujoс╣гa, d), esp. because the four p─Бdas are otherwise unified by the opening ─Б╠Бd ├нd. What sets bc off from a,d is the fact that the subjects in b and c are ritual offerings, pakt├нс╕е тАШcooked foodтАЩ and s├│maс╕е respectively, as opposed to the personal subjects (at least in my interpr.) of a and d. What optative function do these verbs express (and do they express the same one): necessity (тАШshouldтАЩ), potentiality, more certain (тАШwouldтАЩ) or less certain (тАШmightтАЩ), possibility (тАШcouldтАЩ), or desire (also тАШwouldтАЩ)? My surmise is that the vs. depicts the beginning and end points of the successful sacrifice that one of the groups of competitors mounts. P─Бda a contains a general description of the sacrifice and implies its start. In d the unnamed subject, in my opinion Indra, shows that the sacrifice has been successful by enjoying the offered soma (the bull, vс╣Ыс╣гabh├бm). The p─Бdas in between describe the qualities of the better sacrifice that our side performs, in contrast to our opponents, and I interpr. the optatives as expressing near-certain possibility. I therefore take riricy─Бt in b as meaning тАШwould leave behind, succeedтАЩ not in a temporal sense (the cooked food is the next course after the offering cake) but in an evaluative one: cooked food is just better than a puroс╕╖─Б┼Ы-. (This seems generally agreed by interpr.; see esp. GeldnerтАЩs n. 5b.) (Note however that the puroс╕╖─Б┼Ы- was probably not eliminated but supplemented, since the successful sacrificer not only cooks cooked food for Indra in 7b but also roasts grains.) Even more important is the mere presence of soma in c. The p─Бda implies that the other side consists of non-pressers (├бsuс╣гv─лn), who therefore cannot offer soma to Indra. Soma is our trump card and leaves our competitors out in the cold, as it were.

(Notice that the non-pressers contrast with the s├║с╣гvi- in 2d. For s├║с╣гvi-/├бsuс╣гvi- as well as pakt├н, see also the next hymn IV.25.6-7.) My tr. of d differs in an important way from Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н). They take y├бjadhyai as an infinitive complement to jujoс╣гa with vс╣Ыс╣гabh├бm as object, though with two different interpretations. GeldnerтАЩs тАЬdann beliebt man einen Stier zu opfernтАЭ (so also Keydana, Inf., p. 289, with disc.) assumes that the vс╣Ыс╣гabh├б- is a sacrificed animal.

Witzel Got┼Н correctly point out that тИЪyaj does not take an acc. of the offering but of the god who receives the offering and therefore take vс╣Ыс╣гabh├б- as referring to Indra. The subj.

in either case must be an unidentified priest or the like. In my view, by contrast, Indra is the unnamed subj., who receives pleasure from the тАШbullтАЩ soma – note that vс╣Ыс╣гabh├б- is an epithet of soma, as well as of Indra and other gods. The y├бjadhyai is a purpose inf. without object, as it generally is (cf., nearby IV.21.5 ├нyarti v─Б╠Бcaс╣Г jan├бyan y├бjadhyai тАЬ(who) raises his speech, giving birth to it in order to carry out the sacrificeтАЭ).

As Oldenberg notes, there are 3 forms of тИЪric in this hymn, all pf.: pf. part.

ririkv─Бс╣Гsaс╕е (3b), pf. opt. riricy─Бt here, and a plupf. (probably) arirec─лt (9c). They are all somewhat marked in form and have different contextual meanings. Oldenberg remarks тАЬder Dichter liebte dies Verb.тАЭ Certainly he seems to be making a point with it.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The pile-up of p─Бda-initial ─Б╠Бd ├нd тАШjust then, just after thatтАЩ, beginning with 4d and marking every p─Бda in 5, conveys the quick succession of events, but switches abruptly from battlefield to sacrifice. The n├йme constructions of 4d and 5a make it clear, however, that despite the change in venue the same antagonists are in play.

Note also the similarity of the predicates of the two n├йme constructions: indrayante тАж indriy├бс╣Г yajante. This is the only occurrence of the denom. indraya- in the RV and it may have been created to serve as a foil for the second VP.

Hence many a one worships the might of Indra: hence let the brew succeed the meal-oblation.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra bestows wealth upon him who offers a libation to him, desiring it, though in another sphere; and, with a humble mind, makes him who is devoted to him his friend in combats.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He [=Indra] makes wide space for the one who presses soma in just this way for Indra who is eager for it.
The man with fully focused mind who never loses the trackтАФjust him does he [=Indra] make his comrade in battles.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The тАЬwide spaceтАЭ theme returns from 2d. The laconic expression of the recipient of wide space in 2d (the dat. s├║с╣гvaye тАШfor the presserтАЩ) is expanded into a dat. pronoun with rel. clause attached: asmai тАж y├б itth├йndr─Бya s├│mam u┼Ыat├й sun├│ti.

Since the first part of this hymn ends with vs. 7, vss. 2 and 6 are symmetrical and this echo forms a small internal ring. But there are no other signs of ring composition.

The tradition (as well as modern ed. and tr.) is split on whether to read ├бvivenam (Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition, M├╝ller ed., S─Бyaс╣Зa., Lubotsky, and AiG I.1.333) or ├бvivenan (Auf. ed., Pp, Grassmann, Ol, and Geldner); see OldenbergтАЩs disc.

Quite apart from the actual form is its referent. Oldenberg, who accepts the ├бvivenan reading, takes c with d and identifies Indra as the referent of ├бvivenan. Although this fits better with the similar expression in the next hymn (IV.25.3) where gods are (or may be) the subject, here I think Geldner is correct that c belongs grammatically with the rel. cl. in ab, and the referent of ├бvivenan is the soma-presser subject of that rel. cl.

This nominative is resumed by the appropriate correlative prn. t├бm in the acc. in d.

06-07 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

The battle/sacrifice trajectory of vss. 4-5 is wrapped up in vss. 6-7, where it is made clear (esp. in 6d) that if you want IndraтАЩs help on the battlefield, you had better perform a good sacrifice, not stinting on the soma.

Griffith

Indra gives comfort to the man who truly presses, for him who longs fot it, the Soma,
Not disaffected, with devoted spirit this man he takes to be his friend in battles.

Geldner

Dem schafft er einen Ausweg, der dem darnach verlangenden Indra den Soma pre├Яt ungeteilten Herzens, nicht unlustig, nur den macht er in den K├дmpfen zu seinem Freund.

Grassmann

Nur dem verschaffet Indra rechten Fortgang, der Soma ihm, dem heischenden bereitet, Mit aufmerksamem Geiste unabl├дssig, den macht er zum Genossen sich in Schlachten.

рдЕрджреНрдп рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рджрд┐рд╡рд╕реЗ рдпрдГ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирдГ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдп рдкрд░рдореИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдп рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдп рд╕реЛрдордВ рд╕реЛрдо рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдордиреНрдирдВ рд╕реБрдирд╡рддреН рд╕реБрдиреБрдпрд╛рддреН рдЕрднрд┐рд╖рд╡рдВ рдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рддреН ред рддрдерд╛ рдпрдГ рдкрдХреНрддреАрдГ рдкрдХреНрддрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдВрд╢реНрдЪ рдкреБрд░реЛрдбрд╛рд╢рд╛рджреАрдиреН рдкрдЪрд╛рддреН рдкрдЪреЗрддреН рдкрдЪрдирдВ рдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рддреН ред рдЙрдд рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рдпрдГ рдзрд╛рдирд╛рдГ рднрд░реНрдЬрдирдпреЛрдЧреНрдпрд╛рди рдпрд╡рд╛рдиреН ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рднреГрд╖реНрдЯреНрдпрд╡рд╡рд╛рдЪреА рдзрд╛рдирд╛рд╢рдмреНрджрд╕реНрддрджреНрдпреЛрдЧреНрдпрдВ рдпрд╡рдорд╛рддреНрд░рдВ рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдпрддрд┐ ред рднреГрдЬрд╛рддрд┐ рднреГрдЬреНрдЬреЗрддреН рднрд░реНрдЬрдирдВ рдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рддреН ред рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдордирд╛рдпреЛрдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрддреЛ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рдЙрдЪрдерд╛рдирд┐ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐ рд╣рд░реНрдпрди рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдХрд╛рдордпрдорд╛рдирдГ рд╕рдиреН рддрд╕реНрдорд┐рди рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдиреЗ рд╡реГрд╖рдгрдВ рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рдгрд╕рдорд░реНрдердВ рд╢реБрд╖реНрдордВ рдмрд▓рдВ рджрдзрддреН рдзрд╛рд░рдпрддрд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra accepting graciously the praises of his devoted (worshipper), who today pours out the libation to him who toasts the buttered cakes, or fries barley for Indra, exercises towards him the power that grants his desires.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Whoever will press soma for Indra today, will cook the cooked foods, and will roast the grainsтАФ
upon him will Indra, gladly receiving the recitations of the zealous one, confer his bullish explosive force.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The ┼Ы├║с╣гma- that Indra confers on the sacrificer is the тАШexplosive forceтАЩ that will help him (both Indra and the mortal aided by him) prevail in battle.

The battle/sacrifice trajectory of vss. 4-5 is wrapped up in vss. 6-7, where it is made clear (esp. in 6d) that if you want IndraтАЩs help on the battlefield, you had better perform a good sacrifice, not stinting on the soma.

Griffith

He who this day for Indra presses Soma, prepares the brew and fries the grains of barley-
Loving the hymns of that devoted servant, to him may Indra give heroic vigour.

Geldner

Wer heute dem Indra Soma pressen und Kochspeisen kochen und K├╢rner r├╢sten wird, dem wird Indra bullenhafte Kampfwut verleihen, indem er des Dichtenden Loblieder gern annimmt.

Grassmann

Wer heute Soma keltert f├╝r den Indra, ihm Br├╝hen kocht und ihm die K├╢rner r├╢stet, Wer Lust hat an des frommen Dichters Spr├╝chen, dem schenket Indra heldengleiche St├дrke.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen the destroyer (of enemies) distinguishes a mortal foe; when the lord is engaged in the long (continued) battle, (his) bride summons to the dwelling the showerer (of benefits), encompassed by the offerers of the libation.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

When the lord is engaged in the long battle: d─лrgham yad ─Бjim abhyakhyad arya: arya = sv─Бmi, lord, i.e., Indra; patn─л in the next verse is Indra’s wife

Jamison Brereton

When the ballsy one surveyed the clash, when he looked upon the long (war)drive of the stranger,
his wife roared the bull (back) into the house, though he had been
whetted sharp by the soma pressers.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Both Geldner and Oldenberg suggest that с╣Ы╠Бgh─Бv─Б should be read as neut. *с╣Ы╠Бgh─Бvad on the basis of similar (but not identical) X.27.3 yad─Б╠Бv─Б╠Бkhyat sam├бraс╣Зam с╣Ы╠Бgh─Бvad. This seems unnec., since nom. sg. с╣Ы╠Бgh─Бv─Б makes fine sense, and, as anyone who has tangled with it knows, X.27 is a very strange hymn. The only factor in favor of the emendation is the fact that с╣Ы╠Бgh─Бv─Б is the only representative of the -van-stem с╣Ы╠Бgh─Бvan-; otherwise we find the -vant-stem с╣Ы╠Бgh─Бvant- (3x). But -van- and -vantstems coexist elsewhere – cf. magh├бvan(t)- – and eliminating the -van-stem here doesnтАЩt seem sufficient reason to make the emendation. (Note that Witzel Got┼Н do not follow Geldner and Oldenberg, and Geldner allows for the possibility of the nom. in his n. 8a.) Geldner suggests that the subjects of a and b might be IndraтАЩs wife. Scarlatta (616 and n.

  1. has her as the subj. of b but not a. After surveying the various possibilities in his n. he says, with remarkable understatement, тАЬDas Dramolett l├дsst Raum f├╝r verschiedene Interpretationen.тАЭ I think it likely that Indra is the subj. of the first two p─Бdas both because the word p├бtn─л is only introduced in the 3rd p─Бda and because one wonders whether a woman would be in a position to survey the battlefield.

In d тАЬwhetted sharp by the soma pressersтАЭ (n├н┼Ыitaс╣Г somas├║bhiс╕е) continues the theme of the previous vss., that getting Indra on oneтАЩs side in battle requires plying him with soma at the sacrifice.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬA man has realized a small price for an article of great value, and again coming (to the buyer he says) this has not been sold; I require the full price; but he does not recover a small price by a large (equivalent); whether helpless or clever they adhere to their bargain.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

A man has realized: bh┼лyas─Б vasnam acarat kan─лyas = liс╣н, by much a man acquires a little, wealth or value; ka┼Ыcid paс╣Зyena dravyeс╣Зa alpataram m┼лlyam pr─Бpnoti: ka┼Ыcit is understood to be the vendor; one (a vendor) who takes a small price for valuable goods, comes afterwards to the buyer, and says, this has not been sold by me, and, so saying, he requires the balance of the price; but he, the vendor, does not recover the full price, nor does he get back the article; according to the bargain between them it may not be otherwise; the sale has taken plural ce, and if the bargain has been kept, then it has only to be considered that such is the object of the price, and that is the conclusion: a baragin has been made, and the (stipulated) price given; therefore, in the first plural ce, an agreement is to be made by me: so reflecting, V─Бmadeva, having by much praise got Indra into his possession or subjugation, purposes to make a bargain when about to dispose of him, as in the next verse

Jamison Brereton

[Indra:] тАЬWith a greater price he got a lesser deal. Unsold, I took pleasure in going (home) again.
He did not replace the lesser with a greater. Skimpy skills milk the
bargain [?] dry.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, this vs. introduces the vocabulary of commerce, which is otherwise little represented in our texts (though see AV┼Ъ III.15, called by Whitney тАЬFor success in tradeтАЭ) and therefore difficult to get a handle on. My interpr.

differs on some important points from the standard (Oldenberg, Geldner, Witzel Got┼Н, K├╝mmel [425]). In p─Бda a most interpr. take k├бn─лyaс╕е тАШlesserтАЩ as referring to the price and bh┼л╠Бyas─Б тАШgreaterтАЩ as what is being bought. But price is always in the instr.: see in the next vs. 10ab da┼Ы├бbhiс╕е тАж dhen├║bhiс╕е. Therefore, grammar requires us to conclude that, rather than complaining that the potential purchaser offered too little for that very valuable asset, Indra himself, Indra is protesting that the purchaser went for an inferior product (another god?) with too high an offer. In p─Бdas b and c he further points out that the purchaser failed to take advantage of the chance to buy Indra (who therefore went away тАШunsoldтАЩ ├бvikr─лtaс╕е) and to leave behind (/replace) the poor bargain he made in the first place.

As also indicated in the published introduction, I take p─Бda d as an old saying encapsulating the wisdom of not wasting your money on a substandard item. The problem in this p─Бda is v─Бс╣З├бm, which ordinarily means тАШvoice, musicтАЩ (see EWA s.v.).

However, Geldner tr. тАШHandelтАЩ and suggests (n. 9d) that it is derived from vaс╣З├нj- тАШmerchantтАЩ, which seems very plausible. That it is otherwise unknown in this meaning would not be surprising, given the specialized lexical level it inhabits.

Griffith

He bid a small price for a thing of value: I was content, returning, still unpurchased.
He heightened not his insufficient offer. Simple and clever, both milk out the udder.

Geldner

F├╝r H├╢heres macht er ein niedrigeres Tauschgebot. Ich war froh, als ich unverkauft wieder ging. Das niedrigere ersetzte er nicht durch ein h├╢heres. Schwache Geister verderben sich den Handel.

Grassmann

F├╝r das, was mehr werth war, bot man einen geringeren Kaufpreis; ich war, als ich heim ging, froh, den Handel nicht gemacht zu haben; ein anderer liess das, was weniger werth war, nicht f├╝r einen h├╢heren Preis ab; geringe Einsicht melkt ganz das Euter aus [d.h. Thoren wollen aus allem den h├╢chsten Vortheil ziehen.]

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬWho buys him, my Indra, with ten kine? when he shall have slain (your) foes, then let (the purchaser) give him again to me.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

[IndraтАЩs wife:] тАЬWho buys this Indra of mine with ten cows,
when heтАЩs going to smash obstacles? Then will he return him to me
again?тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

The big question about this vs. is the identity of the speaker. The standard view is that it is the poet V─Бmadeva, who is putting Indra on sale temporarily, with the requirement that he be returned after his obstacle-smashing is done. I find this unlikely. How did Indra come to be possessed by V─Бmadeva (im├бm тАж m├бm├йndram тАЬthis Indra of mineтАЭ)? Who is he hawking Indra to? Why has the scene changed from the domestic one of Indra and his wife to, presumably, the ritual ground? My own suggestion, albeit somewhat tentative, is that the speaker is IndraтАЩs wife. Who would have a better right to call him тАЬthis Indra of mineтАЭ? Moreover, there seems no good reason to introduce his wife as an emphatic actor in vs. 8 and then drop her out of the story. Since the three vss. seem unified in tone and theme, common sense suggests that they should take place in the same location with the same actors.

The standard tr. take c with d, e.g., Geldner: тАЬWenn er die Feinde erschlagen hat, so soll er ihn mir zur├╝ckgeben.тАЭ The problem with this is that it assumes an anterior, specifically future anterior, value тАЬ(will) have smashedтАЭ for the intensive subjunctive j├бс╣Еghanat. For this reason I attach it to ab. However, it may make more sense to allow the future anterior and make the yad─Б╠Бclause the prior condition for the return in p─Бda d. In this case the tr. would be тАЬWho buys this Indra of mine with ten cows? When he [=Indra] will have smashed the obstacles, then will he [=buyer] return him [=Indra] to me?тАЭ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬGlorified (in the past), glorified, Indra, at present, satisfy your worshipper with food, as rivers (are filled with water); lord of horses, a new hymn has been made for you; may we, possessed of chariots, be ever diligent in your praise.тАЭ

тАУ Now praised, o Indra, now being sung, make refreshment swell for the singer like rivers.
A new sacred formulation has been made for you, o you of the fallow bays. Through our insightful thought may we be charioteers who
always win.

Griffith

Now, Indra! lauded, glorified with praises, let wealth swell high like rivers for the singer.
For thee a new hymn, Lord of Bays, is fashioned. May we, car-borne, through song be victors ever.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдлрд┐рд░ рдЙрд╕реА рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд╣рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рд╣рд░рд┐рд╡рдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рднреГрддреНрдпреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдпреБрдХреНрдд (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдп рдХреА рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрд╛ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ ! рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛ ! рдпрджрд┐ рдЖрдк рд▓реЛрдЧ рдзрди рдХреА рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрд╛ рдХрд░реЛ рддреЛ рдзрд░реНрдореНрдордпреБрдХреНрдд рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрде рд╕реЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛ рдХреЛ рдирд┐рд░рдиреНрддрд░ рдХрд░реЛ реерезрезрее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд░реНрдпрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдХреЗ рдкреБрддреНрд░ рдХреА рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛, рдЕрдзрд░реНрдо рдХреЗ рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧ рд╕реЗ рдФрд░ рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдХрд░реНрдо рд╕реЗ рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐ рдФрд░ рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдп рдХреА рд╡реГрджреНрдзрд┐, рдирд┐рдпрдорд┐рдд рдЖрд╣рд╛рд░ рд╡рд┐рд╣рд╛рд░, рд╢рддреНрд░реБ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд┐рдЬрдп рдФрд░ рдЬреНрдпреЗрд╖реНрда рдХрдирд┐рд╖реНрда рдХрд╛ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░ рдЦрд╛ рдЧрдпрд╛, рдЗрд╕ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдЗрд╕ рд╕реЗ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ реерезрезрее рдпрд╣ рдЪреМрдмреАрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рдмрд╛рд░рд╣рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рд╣рд░рд┐рд╡ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ ! рд╕реНрддреБрддреЛ рдЧреГрдгрд╛рдирд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рдЬрд░рд┐рддреНрд░реЗ рдирджреНрдпреЛ рдиреЗрд╖рдВ рдиреБ рдкреАрдкреЗрд╕реНрддрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреНрддреЗрд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рднрд┐рд░реНрдзрд┐рдпрд╛ рдирд╡реНрдпрдВ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╛рдХрд╛рд░рд┐ рддреНрд╡рдпрд╛ рд╕рд╣ рд░рдереНрдпрдГ рд╕рджрд╛рд╕рд╛ рд╡рдпрдореИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпрдиреНрддреЛ рдиреБ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдиреБ) рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрднрдпрддреНрд░ рдЛрдЪрд┐ рддреБрдиреБрдШреЗрддрд┐ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГред (рд╕реНрддреБрддрдГ) рд╢реБрджреНрдзрд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░реЗрдг рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рддрдГ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫреБрдХ (рдиреБ) (рдЧреГрдгрд╛рдирдГ) рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдердВ рд╕реНрддреБрд╡рдиреН (рдЗрд╖рдореН) рдЕрдиреНрдирдореН (рдЬрд░рд┐рддреНрд░реЗ) рдпрд╛рдЪрдорд╛рдирд╛рд╜рдпрд╛рдЪрд┐рддрд╛рдп рд╡рд╛ (рдирджреНрдпрдГ) рд╕рд░рд┐рддрдГ (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рдкреАрдкреЗрдГ) рд╡рд░реНрджреНрдзрдп (рдЕрдХрд╛рд░рд┐) рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрддреЗ (рддреЗ) рддрд╡ (рд╣рд░рд┐рд╡рдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рддрднреГрддреНрдпрдпреБрдХреНрдд (рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо) рдорд╣рджреНрдзрдирдореН (рдирд╡реНрдпрдореН) рджреЗрд╢рджреЗрд╢рд╛рдиреНрддрд░рд╛рджреН рджреНрд╡реАрдкрджреНрд╡реАрдкрд╛рдиреНрддрд░рд╛рджреНрд╡рд╛ (рдзрд┐рдпрд╛) рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░рдЬреНрдЮрдпрд╛ рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрдпрд╛ рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБ рдХреГрддреЗрди рдХрд░реНрдореНрдордгрд╛ рд╡рд╛ (рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо) рднрд╡реЗрдо (рд░рдереНрдпрдГ) рдмрд╣реБрд░рдерд╛рджрд┐рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдГ (рд╕рджрд╛рд╕рд╛рдГ) рднреГрддреНрдпреИрдГ рд╕рд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдГ реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ ! рдпрджрд┐ рдпреВрдпрдВ рдзрдирдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдд рддрд░реНрд╣рд┐ рдзрд░реНрдореНрдпреЗрдг рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рдпреЛрдЧреНрдпрд╛рдВ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдВ рд╕рддрддрдВ рдХреБрд░реБрддреЗрддрд┐ реерезрезрее рдЕрддреНрд░ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд░реНрдпрд╡рддрдГ рдкреБрддреНрд░рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛рд╜рдзрд░реНрдорддреНрдпрд╛рдЧреЗрди рд╕реБрдХрд░реНрдордгрд╛ рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮреИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдзрдирдВ рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рд╜рд╣рд╛рд░рд╡рд┐рд╣рд╛рд░рдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрд╡рд┐рдЬрдпреЛ рдЬреНрдпреЗрд╖реНрдардХрдирд┐рд╖реНрдард╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░рд╢реНрдЪреЛрдХреНрддреЛрд╜рдд рдПрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ реерезрезрее рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдорд╛рдгрд╕рд╛рдВрдиреЛ! рдЬрд░ рддреБрдореНрд╣рд╛рд▓рд╛ рдзрдирд╛рдЪреА рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрд╛ рдЕрд╕реЗрд▓ рддрд░ рдзрд░реНрдордпреБрдХреНрдд рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреЗ рд╕рддрдд рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛ рдХрд░рд╛. рее резрез рее
